=500  \\$aPieter Burman the Elder (Utrecht 1668 - Leiden 1741) a Dutch classical scholar, was appointed Extraordinary Professor of Eloquence and Poetry in Utrecht in 1696.  In 1715 he held the office of Professor of History, Eloquence and Greek Languages in Leiden. He was highly esteemed by the poets of his time but he had also made many enemies because of his sharp pen. For example, he never missed an opportunity to denounce the clergy. In 1711, he took up arms against the theater-hostile Utrecht clergy. His "Speech for the Comedy," which first appeared in Latin, resulted in 13 pamphlets.

=500  \\$aPieter Burman the Elder (Utrecht 1668 - Leiden 1741) a Dutch classical scholar, was appointed Extraordinary Professor of Eloquence and Poetry in Utrecht in 1696. In 1715 he held the office of Professor of History, Eloquence and Greek Languages in Leiden. He was highly esteemed by the poets of his time but he had also made many enemies because of his sharp pen. For example, he never missed an opportunity to denounce the clergy. =336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aJohan de Crane belonged to a not inconsiderable family, that flourished for a long time in Zeeland. He was born February 23rd 1676, and after good school and academy education, on March 13th 1696 became a minister, he was called to Nisse, and confirmed there April 7th 1697, from where he left for Oostkapelle in 1703. His health forced him to ask for an honorable resignation in 1727, which was granted. After that time he lived in Middelburg, but still frequently visited the pulpit, both there and in his last congregation; he even had the rare privilege of being able to confirm his six successors in Oostkapelle over a period of nineteen years. He died in Middelburg on the 31st of December 1746.

=100  \\$aRoubo, André Jacob$d1739-1791$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q2847056$96233
=245  \\$aL'Art du menuisier
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aParis$bAcadémie royale des sciences$c1769-74
=300  \\$a5 vols. (1312+276+170 pages)$billustrations, folded pages
=500  \\$aAndré Jacob Roubo (1739-1791) was a master carpenter and cabinetmaker His 's comprehensive four-part treatise L’Art du Menuisier (The Art of the Carpenter) was published between 1769 and 1775 by the Académie des Sciences.The original four-volume work consisted of 1066 pages in total and many hundreds of plates which were engraved by Roubo himself. Sometimes colloquially referred to as "The Roubo", it is considered even today as the best guide for traditional joinery. It develops and discusses in detail the technical knowledge of carpentry that was under Louis XV in its heyday.  
=500  \\$aL’Art du Menuisier is divided into four volumes:
07G01_1: Première partie (building joinery part I) – this part covers basic geometry, types of wood, profiles, assemblages, tools, mobile joinery, shutters and wickets, crosses, and doors; Seconde partie (building joinery part II) – this part covers flooring (including parquetry), panelling, interior decoration, liturgical furniture, installation and assembly of joinery, arches and curves, and stairs.
07G01_2: Troisième partie (specialty woodwork) – the third part consist of three discrete sections: coach construction, furniture, and 
07G01_3: cabinetmaking. Quatrieme partie (garden woodwork) – this part covers the fundamentals of outdoor woodwork and deals with trellis, pilasters & columns, vases & flowerpots; Essaie, Conclusion, Table Alphabetique.
07G01_4: Plates
07G01_5: Plates

=041  \\$afre
=100  \\$aFuretière, Antoine$d1619-1688$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q586211$96238
=245  \\$aDictionnaire universel,$bcontenant generalement tous les mots françois tant vieux que modernes, et les termes de toutes les sciences et des arts
=250  \\$a4th ed.
=260  \\$aThe Hague$bs.n.$c1727
=300  \\$a4 vols. (unpaginated)$btitle pages in red and black ink
=520  \\$aThe 'Dictionnaire universel' was a dictionary and encyclopedia compiled by Antoine Furetière and published posthumously in 1690. Unlike the rival dictionary of the Académie française, finally published in 1694, Furetière's 'Dictionnaire' included specialized technical and scientific vocabulary. It was also an encyclopedia of sorts in dealing with things as well as words. Despite having been banned in France, it was a commercial success and exerted an enormous influence on eighteenth-century French dictionaries and encyclopedias. It continued to be edited and republished through 1727 (this edition).
=534  \\$aOriginally published in 1690
=590  \\$aOu l'on explique tout ce qui concerne la philosophie; logique & physique; la medecine ou anatomie; pathologie, therapeutique, chirurgie, pharmacie, chymie, botanique; ou l’histoire naturelle des plantes, & celle des animaux, mineraux, metaux & pierreries, & celle des drogues naturelles & artificielles. La mythologie, et l'antiquité sacree et profane, la theologie naturelle, positive, scholastique, morale & mystique; la jurisprudence civile & canonique, feodale & municipale, & celle des ordonnances. Les mathematiques; la geometrie, l’arithmetique, & l’algebre; la trigonometrie, geodesie, ou l’arpentage, l'astronomie, l’astrologie, la gnomonique, la geographie; la musique, l'optique, catoptrique, dioptriquè, & perspective; l'architecture civile & militaire, la pyrotechnie, tactique, & statique. Les arts; la rhetorique, la poesie, la grammaire, la peinture, sculpture, &c. la marine, le manege, la danse, l’eserime, le blason, la venerie, la fauconnerie, la pêche, l’agriculture, l'oeconomie, & les arts mechaniques. Avec les termes de relations d’orient & d'occident, la qualité des poids, mesures & monnoyes; les etimologies des mots, l’invention des choses, & l'origine de proverbes, & leur relation à ceux des autres langues. Les remarues des auteurs qui ont traité de la langue françoise & plusieurs traits d'histoires, curiositez naturelles, & setences morales, qui sont raportées pour donner des exemples de phrases & de constructions. Le tout extrait des plus excellens auteurs anciens & modernes.

=100  \\$aAlbrechtsberger, Johann Georg$d1736-1809$4aut$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q314164$95150

=490  \\$aAlbrechtsberger's Werke
=500  \\$aEngraved frontispiece showing the portrait of Albrechtsberger
=500  \\$aDeidcated to Freyherrn Joseph von Pasqualati und Osterberg
=520  \\$aJohann Georg Albrechtsberger (1736-1809) was an Austrian composer and organist who enjoyed a wide reputation as music theorist, teaching Ludwig van Beethoven, Ignaz von Seyfried, Johann Nepomuk Hummel, Ignaz Moscheles, Anton Reicha, Franz Xaver Wolfgang Mozart, and Josef Weigl. In 1792, he became Kapellmeister of St. Stephen's Cathedral instead of Mozart, who had passed away. Possibly the most valuable service he rendered to music was in his theoretical works. In 1790 he published at Leipzig a treatise on composition, of which a third edition appeared in 1821. An English version of this was published by Novello in 1855. His compositional style derives from the counterpoint of Johann Joseph Fux, who was Kapellmeister at St Stephen's Cathedral from 1713 to 1741. Ignaz von Seyfried (1776-1841), who edited Albrechtsberger's works, was also a keyboard student of Mozart.

=041  \\$aita
=100  \\$aGervasoni, Carlo$d1762-1819$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q16268404$95553
=245  \\$aLa scuola della musica
=260  \\$aPiacenza$bOrcese$c1800
=300  \\$a2 vols. (552-[2]+100 pages)
=500  \\$aCarlo Gervasoni was an Italian organist, violinist and composer, as well as a harpsichordist, philosopher and music theorist who is best known for this treatise as well as his 'Nuova teoria di musica ricavata dall'odierna pratica' (1812; see 04G21), which helped lay the foundations for sonata form theory.
=500  \\$aThe music examples are bound in with the 'Carteggio musicale' (08B23)
=500  \\$aThe title page contains a portrait of the author
=520  \\$aGervasoni studied every form of song, instrument, and related work available, and found there was not enough written for musicians of the day. This inspired him to write about music in a way that was accessible to anyone. After ten years of hard work he published 'The school of music' in 1800, an important treatise which was, however, harshly criticized by contemporaries for the excessive simplification of some concepts and the practice of contrapuntal composition on new melodies rather than on ancient melodies of the cantus firmus. Gervasoni's treatise of 1800 is particularly important because it defines fundamental guidelines for modulations in the sonata form, defined later only from 1816 by Reicha and subsequently by Carl Czerny.

Mechanismus oder Neue Abhandlung von der künstlichen Zusammensetzung des Menschliche Auges und den besonderen Nutzen desselben, sowohl vor sich, als in Absicht der anliegen Theile, Nebst Seiner Art, dessen Krankheiten zu heilen, Wie er solche bey einer mehr als zwanzigjährigen Erfahrung seiner durch Europa glücklich gethanen Augencuren bewährt befunden.
Mit den dazu gehörigen Kupfertafeln, Unter Königlich - Pohlnisch - und Chur-Sächsicher allergnädigsten Freyheit, und ausdrücklichen Bewilligung des Verfassers in Deutsche übersetzt.

It is a satirical attack on superstitions, other traditions of European society and on the Western Church.

=260  \\$aParis$bBallard$c1739
=300  \\$axxxiii-178 pages$boblong, leather bound embossed in gold, marbled endpapers
=500  \\$aDardanus is a tragédie en musique in a prologue and five acts. It premiered at the Paris Opéra on 19 November 1739 to mixed success, mainly because of the dramatic weakness of the libretto. This caused Rameau and La Bruère to rework the opera, completely rewriting the last three acts, for a revival in 1744. Only when Dardanus was again performed in 1760 did it win acclaim as one of Rameau's greatest works.

=500  \\$aThe eight collections of Nouvelles poésies spirituelles et morales were published in Paris by Guillaume Desprez, Jean Desessartz, Philippe-Nicolas Lottin and Guichard from 1730 to 1737. This collection of more than four hundred spiritual parodies in French for voice and continuo, borrowed from seventy composers, was a great success in the 18th century, as shown by the reprints that were made.
=500  \\$aon music by Lully, Destouches, Desmarets, Clerambault, Bernier, Lambert, Beaupré, Gillier, Campra, Bertin, Marchand, Couperin, Marais, Debousset and others

=500  \\$aparodied genres are operas, detached arias, cantatas and instrumental pieces
=500  \\$athe Fables of de la Fontaine, always separately paginated, are parodied on Vaudevilles and 'petits Airs aisés à chanter' and could be accompanied by the harpsichord and the musette
=500  \\$avarious songs in different categories: Louanges de Dieu, Misteres de Notre Seigneur J. C., Vertus, Vices, Les IV Fins de l'homme, Fables (by de la Fontaine)

=100  \\$aWinter, Nicolaas Simon van$d1718-1795$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q2697615$95934
=245  \\$aDe Amstelstroom
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bMeijer$c1755
=300  \\$a[34]-207 pages$boriginal period binding, leather back with red label and gilt lettering
=500  \\$aNicolaas Simon van Winter (1718-1795) was, besides playwright and poet, salesman in pigments.
=500  \\$aContains a touching autograph dedication by the author to a granddaughter by law: Cornelia Christina van Orsoy, dating from his last years (and indeed clearly written by an elderly person). 
=500  \\$aCornelia Christina van Orsoy was a daughter of Anna Louisa van der Poorten (1742-1800), who married Pieter van Winter in 1780, thus becominging part of the Van Winter family.  
Pieter van Winter was the son of Nicolaas Simon van Winter and his first wife Johanna Muhl. After Johanna's death Nicolaas had married poet Lucretia van Merken, the couple had later moved from Amsterdam to Leiden. Apperently Lucretia had been fond of Cornelia and had wanted to give her this book. 
=500  \\$aDe Amstelstroom is an ode to the river Amstel.
=500  \\$aContains an engraved frontispiece, (with explanation), engraving on titlepage and a beautiful fold-out map of the Amstel (Pieter Meijer 1755).
=561  \\$aEx libris Cornelia Christina van Orsoy (ms dedication by author)
=561  \\$aDedication: "Aan Cornelia Christina van Orsoy worden de Dichtwerken van Nicolaas Simon van Winter en wijlen Lucretia Wilhelmina van Merken, (tot welken zij door Gods Voorzienigheid de betrekking van grootouderen bekomen heeft) geschonken; (ook volgens begeerte van haare Grootmoeder;) ten liefde blijke, en tot gedachtenis haarer Grootouderen. Leyden, den 19 APril 1791, Nicolaas Simon van Winter"

=041  \\$afre
=100  \\$aBonneval, Michel de$d? - 1766$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q3311139$4aut$96652
=245  \\$aLes Romans. $bBallet héroïque
=260  \\$aParis$bBallard$c1736
=300  \\$aviii-65-[1] pages$bmarbled paper cover,  engraved title page
=500  \\$aAs general controller of the silverware and intendant of the king's Menus-Plaisirs, Bonneval - choreographer, librettist and production dramatist - was responsible for spending on clothes and furniture, and for organising balls, fêtes, masquerades, carousels, etc. He composed many of the operas performed at court, on the Versailles stage.
=500  \\$aFirst performed in 1736, music by Jean-Baptiste Niel (1690 – 1775) Master of music and batteur de mesure at the Opéra. In 1736 he secured a licence to write keyboard works, which have now disappeared. He performed with some success at the Concert-Spirituel, but he was most famous for composing opera-ballets or heroic ballets such as Les Romans (1736, lyrics by Bonneval) or L'École des amants (1744). The former was a great success, and was performed at court in front of the Queen in 1737. The music, however, was not very personal, and borrowings from Rameau were notable. We have a score in which the composer explains that he has introduced a new accent on the e, between the silent e and the open e, as well as new signs for the figured bass.
=534  \\$aPremiered at the Académie royale de musique on 23 August 1736

=041  \\$afre
=100  \\$aBacilly, Bertrand de$dc. 1625-1690$4aut$4col$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q2899715$96686
=245  \\$aRecueil des plus beaux vers qui ont esté mis en chant
=260  \\$aParis$bSercy, de$c1661
=300  \\$a[xxx]-536 pages$bengraved frontispiece
=500  \\$aFirst of ten such collections published between 1661 and 1680.
=500  \\$aOriginally dedicated to the superintendent Nicolas Fouquet; but after his disgrace, the dedication was quickly replaced by another to Paul Pellisson-Fontanier, Fouquet's secretary. 
=500  \\$aCollection compiled by Benigne de Bacilly, priest and composer, comprising 498 pieces of verse set to song, 277 of which are signed. Many of them appear here for the first time, including 18 by Benserade, 5 by Boisrobert, 68 by Bouillon, 12 by Pellisson, 9 by Scarro, and 5 by Segrais. The airs are by Le Camus, Lambert, Bacilly, Dassoucy, Batiste, Boesset, Moulinié etc. The poems are arranged in alphabetical order of the incipits.
=520  \\$aThe collections of "verses mis en chant" published by Bacilly constitute a very rich compilation of the airs that were sung in Paris in the 1660's. They constitute very interesting documentation because, although published without music, they mention both the name of the poet author of the verses and the name of the musician who set them to music. About ten of these collections were published between 1661 and 1671 by Charles de Sercy, Étienne Loyson, Guillaume de Luyne, Robert III Ballard or Bacilly himself.

=245  \\$aVermischte Gedichte
=260  \\$aLeipzig$bs.n.$c1769
=300  \\$a[xiv]-120 pages
=336  \\$abook
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aContains 'Das Vorspiel , ein Satirische Episches Gedicht in fünf Büchern', a satirical-epic poem directed against Gottsched, originally published 1742, 
The volume also contains Rost's erotic-gallant poem "Der Brautnacht"(The Weddingnight)  (originally published as 'Die schöne Nacht' in 1754) one of those poems for which Rost was more notorious than famous and which "drove the fair blush of shame on virginal cheeks"
The two remaining poems, 'Der fröhliche Jüngling' and 'Die Nachtigall' , are not by Rost, but by J.Fr. Lamprecht and Chr. N. Neumann respectively.

=041  \\$adut$alat
=245  \\$aBrief van Bernardus Forckenbeck aen Iacobum Omphalium; Brief van Bernardus Forckenbeck aen Henricum Welsingium; Brief van Jacobus Omphalius aen Aemilium Trebatium
=260  \\$aDeventer et al.$bs.n.$c1611
=300  \\$a32 pages
=336  \\$abook
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aBernardus Forckenberg, together with Henricus Welsing and Jacobus Omphalius, commissioned the anonymous book 'Officio hominis Christini', which defended the doctrines of Socinianism and advised the reader to join the Polish Socinians without delay. Socinianism is a Non-trinitarian Christian belief system named after the Italian theologians Lelio Sozzini (Latin: Laelius Socinus) and Fausto Sozzini (Latin: Faustus Socinus), which was developed among the Polish Brethren in the Polish Reformed Church during the 16th and 17th centuries. The Socinian booklet, defending Conrad Vorstius (1569-1622) a German-Dutch heterodox Remonstrant theologian, caused an uproar in Friesland. Even before the Frisian justice system could arrest the perpetrators, the three Vorstius-adepts made their way to Steinfurt.

=100  \\$aBosch Kemper, Jeronimo de$d1808-1876$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q2271540$96746
=245  \\$aDirk Rafaelsz Camphuizen, de vrije evangelie-belijder in het tijdvak van het kerkelijk gezang
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bWitkamp$c1872
=300  \\$a32 pages
=336  \\$abook
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aDirk Rafelsz Camphuysen (1586-1627) was a Dutch painter, poet and theologian. Camphuysen left a translation of the Psalms, and a number of short pieces of poetry. He was also author of several theological works, among which is a Compendium Doctrinae Sociniorum. He was relatively successful as a minister, but he had embraced the doctrines of Arminianism, and like other Arminians or Remonstrants, he was banned from ministry and teaching and driven into exile (1619).The Remonstrants is a Protestant movement that had split from the Dutch Reformed Church in the early 17th century. The early Remonstrants supported Jacobus Arminius, and after his death, continued to maintain his original views called Arminianism against the proponents of Calvinism.

=245  \\$aMémoires de Messire Pierre de Bourdeille, Seigneur de Brantôme$c1-2/4
=260  \\$aLeiden$bSambix$c1699
=300  \\$a2 vols. ([iv]-308 + [iv]-304 pages)$b  $c8,5 x 14 cm
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aThere also exists a fourth volume, see https://archive.org/details/mmoirescontenan00brangoog/page/n8
=500  \\$avol.3 = 09F22
=500  \\$aPierre de Bourdeille was a French historian, soldier and biographer.
=500  \\$aDe Bourdeille can hardly be regarded as a historian proper, and his Memoirs cannot be accepted as a very trustworthy source of information. But he writes in a quaint conversational way, pouring forth his thoughts, observations or facts without order or system, and with the greatest frankness.
His works give a picture of the general court-life of the time, with its unblushing and undisguised profligacy. There is not an homme illustre or a dame galante in all his gallery of portraits who has not engaged in sexual immorality; and yet the whole is narrated with the most complete unconsciousness that there is anything objectionable in their conduct.
[Chisholm, Hugh, ed. (1911). "Pierre de Bourdeille, Seigneur and Abbé de Brantôme". Encyclopædia Britannica. 4 (11th ed.). Cambridge University Press.]

=041  \\$alat
=100  \\$aSecundus, Johannes$d1511-1536$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q614229$96787
=245  \\$aOpera accurato recognita ex Museo P. Scriverii
=260  \\$aLeiden$bHeger, de$c1631
=300  \\$a[xxviii]-385 pages$b2 engravings, bound in white vellum
=336  \\$abook
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$a Engraved title page with portrait medallion ("vatis amatoris iulia sculpta manu"); author's portrait on verso of tenth preliminary leaf. 
=500  \\$aJan Everaerts (Secundus) was a New Latin poet of Dutch nationality. He wrote elegies, epigrams, odes, epistles, epithalimia, itineraries, and other prose. His most famous work was Liber Basiorum (Book of Kisses) which is among the works in this volume (p.79-92) The compiler, Peter Schrijver (Scriverius) was was a Dutch antiquarian, philologist, writer and scholar on the history of Holland and Belgium.
=500  \\$aSecundus was a prolific writer, and in his short life he produced several books of elegies on his lovers Julia and Neaera, epigrams, odes, verse epistles and epithalamia, as well as some prose writings (epistles and itineraria).
His most famous work, though, was the Liber Basiorum (Book of Kisses, first complete edition 1541), a short collection consisting of nineteen poems in various metres, in which the poet explores the theme of the kiss in relation to his Spanish lover, Neaera.
=500  \\$aScriverius, was a profilic publisher of humanist literature. He collected manuscripts of Neolatine authors from his own time and from the time of early humanism. Based on these, he produced a number of editions, including the Latin poetry of Janus Secundus (first published in 1619).

=041  \\$alat
=100  \\$aAphthonius of Antioch$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q4441106$96823
=245  \\$aProgymnasmata
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bElsevier$c1649
=300  \\$a441-[14] pages$bengraved frontispiece
=500  \\$aProgymnasmata are a series of preliminary rhetorical exercises that began in ancient Greece and continued during the Roman Empire. These exercises were implemented by students of rhetoric, who began their schooling between ages twelve and fifteen. The purpose of these exercises was to prepare students for writing declamations after they had completed their education with the grammarians. There are only four surviving handbooks of progymnasmata, attributed to Aelius Theon, Hermogenes of Tarsus, Aphthonius of Antioch, and Nicolaus the Sophist.
=500  \\$aAphthonius of Antioch was a student of the great sophist Libanius during the second half of the fourth century. This is the most widely used and referenced handbook that became the standard on the practice of progymnasmata. His treatises were combined with rhetorical treatises of Hermogenes on stasis theory and style to create the “Hermogenic Corpus.” 
=500  \\$aIn Aphthonius Progymnasmata, all students were asked to write out each assignment, memorize it, and then perform a class oration. The progymnasmata were taught in order, increasing in difficulty as the course advances. The courses were organized to begin with story-telling and end with making an argument. There was a focus on literature as a supplement to the course, paying close attention to models of rhetoric and literature. The progymnasmata of Aphthonius was first translated to Latin in the fifteenth century by Rudolphus Agricola.

=041  \\$alat
=100  \\$aSallustius$d86 BC-c. 35 BC$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q7170$95745
=245  \\$aCatilina seu Bellum Catilinarum; Iugurtha, seu Bellum Iugurthinum; Historiarum Fragmenta; Fragmenta historicorum veterum
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bIansson$c1647
=300  \\$a[xvi]-310-[34] pages$bbound in white velum, manuscript annotations, engraved titlepage, portrait
=500  \\$amanuscript annotations in French
=500  \\$a Lucius Sergius Catilina was a Roman politician and soldier. He is best known for instigating the Catilinarian conspiracy, a failed attempt to violently seize control of the Roman state in 63 BC.
=500  \\$aDe bello Iugurthino (also: Bellum Iugurthinum) is Sallust's second historical monograph after De coniuratione Catilinae. The work deals with the events of the war waged by Gaius Marius and Lucius Cornelius Sulla Felix in 111-106 BC against the Numidian king Jugurtha and was written around 40 BC. The main theme of the work is not so much the description of the Jugurthine War, but rather the presentation of certain internal political conditions in Rome. Above all, the contrast between the nobility and the plebeians, the unpleasantness of party fights and the civil wars are discussed. At the end of his explanations, Sallust puts forward the thesis that the decline of the commonwealth was due to the politicians' striving for power.

=100  \\$aRosa, Salvator$d1615-1673$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q359421$96831
=245  \\$aSatire ... dedicate a Settano
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bProthomastix$c1694 [?]
=300  \\$a160-[1] pages$bcoloured gilded enpapers, leather bound, embossed gilded spine
=500  \\$aSalvator Rosa is best known today as an Italian Baroque painter, whose romanticized landscapes and history paintings, often set in dark and untamed nature, exerted considerable influence from the 17th century into the early 19th century. In his lifetime he was among the most famous painters, known for his flamboyant personality, and regarded as an accomplished poet, satirist, actor, musician, and printmaker, as well. He was active in Naples, Rome, and Florence, where on occasion he was compelled to move between cities, as his caustic satire earned him enemies in the artistic and intellectual circles of the day.
=500  \\$aOriginally published in Venice, 1658
=500  \\$apirate edition of a forbidden work (see note on fs: "Proibito")
=500  \\$afalse publication year 1664 added in ink on frontispiece
=500  \\$athe first satire deals with 'La musica' (pages 5-25), the following ones with 'La poesia', 'La pittura', 'La guerra', 'La Babilonia', 'L'Invidia', all writen in tercets (see Dante)
=500  \\$aQuinto Settano was the ps. of the poet Lodovico Sergardi (1660-1726), whose own satires were only published in 1694
=500  \\$aThe six satires by the Neapolitan painter and man of letters constitute as many witty invectives against the vices of the century (Music. Poetry, Painting, War, Babylon, Envy). Confused, disoriented, illogical, he jumps from one thing to another, he says and says again; his thought seems poorly formed and elaborated. What Rosa never lacks is the eagerness, the violence, the loquacity, proper to his character .

=500  \\$aEngraved title page with organ, 4 putti playing instruments and singing, and various instruments hanging on the walls
=500  \\$aThe Music-Saal is in fact the second edition of Majer's Museum musicum theoretico practicum, published at Schwabisch Hall in 1732 and reprinted in 1954 as part of Barenreiter's 'Documenta musicologica' facsimile series, with a brief afterword by Heinz Becker
=500  \\$a Majer was organist and Kantor at St. Katharina, Schwabisch Hall, where he spent most of his life. The present work offers the earliest illustration and fingering instructions for the clarinet, which was not very widespread at the time.

=100  \\$aNiedt, Friedrich Erhard$d1674-1708$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q103357$96858
=245  \\$aMusicalisches ABC zum Nutzen der Lehr- und Lernenden
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aHamburg$bSchiller$c1708
=300  \\$a112 pages$coblong
=500  \\$aFriedrich Erhard Niedt (1674-1708) was a jurist, music theorist and composer who studied in Jena, resided for a while in Hamburg and then moved to Copenhagen. His musical guide reflects compositional techniques in the era of J. S. Bach. Niedt also published a three-part 'Musicalische Handleitung' (1700, 1706 abd 1717), the third part of which was published by Mattheson
=500  \\$aCited in Koopman 2019, 5

=100  \\$aBuma, Johannes$d1694 -1756$4aut$96888
=245  \\$aBoere bruiloft, of Het huwelijk van Moddeworst, en Griet Beerdberg
=260  \\$aKnollendam$bs.n.$c1767
=336  \\$abook
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aHighly amusing and very detailed poetical description of a country-wedding, written in rather an indecent language; A farcical play is inserted. Extensive commentaries and some other prose accompany the poem.
=500  \\$aJohannes Buma (Leeuwarden 1694 - Leeuwarden 1756), son of a pharmacist, practised that profession himself for some time, but after his father's death he turned to painting and poetry. De Boere Bruiloft (The Merry Wedding), a satire on various well-known Frisian persons, has a long history: according to the biography that precedes the work, Buma started writing it between the ages of thirty and forty, after which it remained unfinished for sixteen years. At the insistence of friends, he finally completed it. It was only eleven years after his death, when all those involved had died, that the poem was dared to be published to spare the feelings of the dramatis personae still in life.
=500  \\$aBeautiful mezzotint portrait of Buma by R. Jelgerhuis after R. Keyert.
=500  \\$anote in pencil "de koperen platen zijn nooit verschenen", refers to the Koperen Platen (engraved illustrations) mentioned on the title page, but do not appear in the book.

=100  \\$aBidloo, Govert$d1649-1713$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q1397888$96890
=245  \\$aBrieven der gemartelde apostelen
=250  \\$a3rd ed.
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bVisser$c1712
=300  \\$a[xii]-122 pages$billustrations
=500  \\$aReissued several times before Bidloo’s death, the text and plates depict the author’s warning against the seducing power of good food, wine, and other earthly delights. Gruesome suffering shown includes stoning, quartering, beating, burning, and other bodily tortures endured by these saints, as necessary preparation for the next world.
=500  \\$aDramatic engravings of a martyred woman (title page) and the martyred Apostels. Although the plates are not signed, several sources attribute the engravings to the gifted and socially well connected artist, Romeyn de Hooghe (1645–1708). There might have been dissatisfaction with the result because Bidloo writes elsewhere about the artist’s incompetence* and later, the plates for Bidloo’s monumental 'Anatomia humani corporis' (Amsterdam, 1685) were drawn by Gérard de Lairesse (1640–1711), and engraved by Abraham Blooteling (1640–1690) and Peter van Gunst (1659?–1724?).

=041  \\$ager
=100  \\$aGerbert, Martin$d1720-1793$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q66625$96622
=245  \\$aReisen durch Alemannien, Welschland und Frankreich, welche in den Jahren 1759. 1760. 1761 und 1762. angestellet worden
=260  \\$aUlm, Frankfurt, Leipzig$bWohler$c1767
=300  \\$a[xvi]-478-[9]-[18] pages$billustrations, 9 unnumbered pages inserted, some folded
=336  \\$abook
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aSoon after being appointed librarian of the monastery school in St. Blasien, Gerbert was sent on journeys from 1759 to 1762 for further education, which took him to Germany, Italy and France. He collected materials on the history of medieval liturgy and music and on the history of the monasteries and met many important personalities. Since Gerbert was initially entrusted with the administration of the monastery library, he began to study church history. The special object of his investigations became the history of church singing in the Middle Ages. Subsequently, he developed into an important music historian of modern times. His interest in music led to his acquaintance with Christoph Willibald Gluck, who became his friend. In 1760, during his travels, he collected copies of medieval treatises on music history and theory from monastery libraries. In Bologna he became friends with Padre Martini; both exchanged their rich experiences. The first result was the travel report 'Iter Alemannicum'.

=100  \\$aSmith, Robert$4aut$96924
=245  \\$aHarmonics$bor The Philosophy Of Musical Sounds
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aCambridge$bBentham$c1749
=300  \\$axvi-292-[13] pages$billustrations, 25 folded pages
=336  \\$abook
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$afacsimile edition see 05A22
=500  \\$aSmith (1689 - 1768) trained as a mathematician and was Plumian Professor of Astronomy at Cambridge for forty-four years (1716 - 1760). Although his work on harmonics has a mathematical basis, he approaches the problems of tuning keyboard instruments as a musician would. 
=500  \\$a"Music was both Smith's pastime and his other main scientific interest. He was an accomplished performer on several instruments, particularly the violoncello, and possessed a 'correct ear'. In his Harmonics he advocated the mean-tone temperament or method of tuning keyboard instruments. In the same work he contributed to the mathematical theory of music with an extended discussion of equal harmonic intervals." (Geoffrey Canton in the new Oxford DNB)

=250  \\$a1st ed.

=300  \\$a3 vols. (xv-411-[2]+xv-215+xv-207 pages)$bfolded page with musical notation
=500  \\$ainserted folded page (recto-verso) with aria for soprano "Già presso al termine de'suoi martiri" (Largo) violini, corni, viole & basso continuo , text by Metastasio, composer unknown.
=500  \\$aEsteban de Arteaga (1747-1798) fue uno de los muchos españoles que, en su condición de jesuitas, fueron expulsados de su país por Carlos III en 1767. Siguiendo a la mayor parte de este numeroso grupo, se estableció en Italia. Allí escribió Le Rivoluzioni del teatro musicale italiano (Bolonia, 1783-8 y Venecia, 1785-6) un extenso ensayo histórico-crítico sobre la ópera y, en general, sobre toda manifestación teatral-musical desde la Edad Media hasta su tiempo.

=245  \\$aŒuvres de Monsieur Saint-Evremond, Publiées sur ses Manuscrits,$bavec La Vie de l'Auteur
=250  \\$a5th ed.
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bCovens$bMortier$c1739
=300  \\$a5 vols. ([xxxii]-367-[5]-169-[19]+[ii]-460-[12]+[ii]-443-[17]+[iv]-490-[17]+[viii]-418-[6] pages)$b5 engraved frontispieces, 1 inserted engraving
=500  \\$aCharles de Marguetel de Saint-Denis, seigneur de Saint-Évremond (1613-1703) was a French soldier, hedonist, moralist, essayist and literary critic. After 1661, he lived in exile, mainly in England, as a consequence of his attack on French policy at the time of the Peace of the Pyrenees (1659). He is buried in Poets' Corner, Westminster. He wrote for his friends and  never authorised the printing of any of his works during his lifetime, though Barbin in 1668 published an unauthorised collection. But he empowered Des Maizeaux to publish his works after his death, and they were published in London (2 vols., 1705), and often reprinted. Various writings by Evremond online available, see https://onlinebooks.library.upenn.edu/webbin/book/lookupname?key=Saint%2DEvremond%2C%201613%2D1703

=500  \\$aSébastien de Brossard was a French music theorist, composer and collector. His 'Dictionaire de musique' was the first in its type in French. See 16H10 for the first edition.
=590  \\$acontenant une explication des termes grecs, latins, italiens et françois les plus usitez dans la musique... ensemble une table alphabétique des termes françois qui sont dans le corps de l'ouvrage, sous les titres grecs, latins et italiens, pour servir de supplément, un Traité de la manière de bien prononcer, surtout en chantant, les termes italiens, latins et françois, et un catalogue de plus de 900 auteurs qui ont écrit sur la musique en toutes sortes de temps, de pays et de langues...

=245  \\$aLa Verona illustrata$bridotta in compendio, principalmente per uso de' forestieri, con varie aggiunte. $n1-2/2
=260  \\$aVerona$bMoroni$c1771
=300  \\$a2 vols. (LI-[v]-175+173-[6] pages)$binserted folded plates, bound in cardboard cover
=500  \\$aA monumental work dedicated to the history, writers and monuments of Maffei's city: Verona.
=500  \\$a"Verona illustrated reduced in compendium, mainly for the use of foreigners, with various additions"
=500  \\$aIn the present edition for the use of visitors the first volume contains a biography of Maffei, a history of Verona and a description of the ancient Roman amphitheatre, which is illustrated in six plates. The second volume describes and illustrates in seventeen plates some notable sights of the city and its fortifications, and concludes with a brief survey of its literary history.

=500  \\$aThe work is dedicated by 'P.M.' [identified by the RIBA cataloguer as Pietro Montanari, the editor] to Alvise Mocenigo II, Podestà di Verona (1628-1709)
=500  \\$aFrancesco Scipione Maffei was a Venetian writer and art critic,  an antiquarian with a humanist education, and author of many articles and plays.
=500  \\$aSome plates are signed as made by Dall'Acqua.
=500  \\$aSome plates are copied from the 1732 edition, but others are new, e.g. those of the Museo and the Dogana.

=520  \\$aIn the 17th century music in Zürich was dominated by three collegia musica: the first was ‘zum Chorherrensaal’, followed by the ‘ab dem Musiksaal’ (from 1613) and ‘zur deutschen Schule’ (from 1679). Initially they were concerned only with sacred music, but later also performed contemporary German and Italian secular music. The three societies merged in 1812 to form the Allgemeine Musikgesellschaft Zürich (AMGZ), which since 1813 has produced books on musical subjects in a series of ‘Neujahrsblättern’, the successors to a series of New Year collections of polyphonic pieces published by two of the collegia musica from 1685 and 1713 respectively.

=500  \\$aCarl Czerny (1791-1857) was an Austrian composer, teacher, and pianist of Czech origin whose music spanned the late Classical and early Romantic eras. His vast musical production amounted to over a thousand works and his books of studies for the piano are still widely used in piano teaching. He was one of Ludwig van Beethoven's best-known pupils.

=500  \\$aSarganeck's  "Die höchstnöthige Berechnung", published in Züllichau in 1735, is added to Schmidt's book of 1736 , in a continuing pagination (p.601-672)
=500  \\$aGeorg Sarganeck was a pedagogue, grammar school teacher, school inspector and pietist. He was born in Dolní Suchá in the Těšín region, a village in Karviná District, Moravian-Silesian Region, Czech Republic. He studied at the University of Halle. From 1728 to 1730 he worked as a teacher at the Evangelical Jesus School in Těšín, from where he was expelled by Emperor Charles VI because of his pietism. He went to Germany, where he taught at schools in Neustadt an der Aisch and Halle. He is one of the most important personalities of Czech non-Catholic exile literature. 
=500  \\$aTitle page of Sarganeck's book: "Die höchstnöthige Berechnung der Sünden-Schulden deren Grösse und Mannigfaltigkeit gegen die unendliche Versöhnung und Liebe Gottes in Christo Jesu. Anfangs bey einem Schul=Examine, Nun aber zu gemeinsamer Erbauung herausgegeben von George Sarganeck, Rectore der hochfl. Brandenburg=Culmbach. Stadt=Schule zu Neustadt an der Aisch."

=500  \\$aVery little is known about Jan de Regt (1665-1715). He was the eldest son of Michiel Michielsz de Regt, sailmaker, and Lijsbet Jans van Riet, a baker's daughter. The De Regt family lived in the Jordaan where Jan was baptised in the Noorderkerk, and later on the Waal (the Kromme or the Oude, it is not clear). When Jan de Regt registered as a citizen of Amsterdam in 1694, he gave 'merchant' as his profession. This is a vague designation that could indicate anything from shopkeeper to international trader. He was explicitly not a bread-poet, but a leisure poet. His oeuvre is small: occasional poems, a 'In Praise of Amsterdam', a farce (De nachtwachts) and a number of 'Gezangen' (Songs), mostly on everyday subjects, such as 'Knorhanen gegeten' (Roosters eaten), 'Waar schuil ik voor de lonken' (Where do I hide from the ogres), and 'Al 't gedruis aan ons huis' (All the commotion at our house). Those 'Gezangen' were in fact songs, to be sung to then-familiar tunes like 'En de bok sprong op het geitje'. For the song tune of some others, such as the 'Vechtzang' (poem in praise of the Vecht), De Regt refers to the compositions of 'Sr. Andreas Parchem [= Parcham], given name Musician'. Occasionally, his poets' pen lent itself to current affairs, such as the death of Maria Stuart (1695) and the battle of Oudenaarde (1708). Some noise arose after De Regt's long poem Slechten tyd (1711), to which Jan van Gijsen wrote a counter-poem entitled Goeden tyd. A pamphleteer claimed that the gentlemen had entered into a 'war of poets'. But Van Gijsen vehemently disputed that. Never, he argued, 'was I an enemy of De Regt./ That gentleman never harmed me with works nor with words,/ 'I did sin' so 'I said that I ever heard anything to the man's slander./ I know his good behaviour and praise his poetry,/ which is also ten times as good as mine'. De Regt unfortunately kept quiet on the matter. Jan de Regt died as a 'young man' or bachelor in Amsterdam.

=100  \\$aRicchinius, Thomas Augustinus$d1695-1762$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q87193344$97129
=245  \\$aIndex Librorum Prohibitorum Ssmi D. N. Benedicti XIV Pontificis Maximi jussu recognitus, atque editus
=260  \\$aParma$bCarmignani$c1783
=300  \\$a315-12-[2] pages$bengraved frontispiece, 
=500  \\$aRicchini, a learned Italian ecclesiastic, was born at Cremona in 1695. At the age of fifteen he entered the Dominican order, devoted himself to poetry, and published at Milan several religious pieces. He afterwards taught theology in the principal houses of his order in Lombardy, and filled the office of prior at Cremona. Called to Rome in 1740, he became in 1749 secretary of the Congregation of the Index and examiner of the bishops. He worked in the service of the Roman censorship and was part of the commission that published the list of forbidden books (L'Indice) in 1750, as well as the later revisions of 1753, 1758, 1763... He enjoyed the favor of Benedict XIV, who often made use of his learning in literary work. In 1759 Ricchini became one of the masters of the pope's palace. He died at Rome in 1762.

=245  \\$aIl teatro alla moda $bosia Metodo sicuro, e facile per ben comporre, & esequire l'opere italiane in musica all'uso moderno
=260  \\$aVenice$bAldiviva Licante$c1722

=500  \\$aA discussion and full English translation is published in Musical Quarterly:

=504  \\$ahttps://it.wikipedia.org/wiki/Il_teatro_alla_moda
=520  \\$a'The Fashionable Theater' is a satirical pamphlet in which its author, the Venetian composer Benedetto Marcello, vents his critical opinions on the milieu of the Italian opera seria in the first decades of the eighteenth century. Virtually every aspect of opera seria and its social environment is mercilessly criticized: the artificiality of plots, the stereotyped format of music, the extravagant scenography and machinery, the inability and venality of composers and poets, the vanity and vulgarity of singers, the avidity of impresarios, the ineptitude of musicians. 

The frontispiece contains several allusions to well-known protagonists of the Venetian theater of the time. For instance, the publisher's name "Aldiviva Licante" refers, by means of anagrams, both to Antonio Vivaldi, then very famous as an opera composer, and to the singer Caterina Canteli. The engraving shows a little boat rowed by a well dressed gentleman. Numerous supplies such as a wine barrel and sacks of flour are lying in the forward part of the boat, at the bow of which stands a bear (representing impressario Orsatti) wearing a wig and waving a little flag. An angel wearing a priest's hat and playing on a diminituive violin occupies the opposite position, hovering over the rudder at the stern, representing Antonio Vivaldi. Underneath the picture follows an imprint, in which every word printed in capitals refers to a composer, singer or other person involved in Venetian opera business.
=534  \\$aOriginally published, anonymously, in 1720

Dedicato dall'autore del libro al compositore di esso. Stampato ne Borghi di Belisania per Aldiviva Licante, all'insegna dell'Orso in Peata. Si vende nella strada del Corallo alla porta del palazzo d'Orlando. Come pure in Milano da Francesco Agnelli.

=041  \\$afre
=100  \\$aEpinay, Louise marquise d'$d1726-1783$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q264254$97132
=245  \\$aMémoires
=260  \\$aParis$bFasquelle$cs.d.
=300  \\$a2 vols. (viii-460+500 pages)
=500  \\$aThe pseudo-memoires of Louise d'Epinay are written in the form of a sort of autobiographic romance, 'L'Histoire de Madame de Montbrillant', begun when she was thirty but never published in her lifetime. It intersperses fictionalized set pieces exhibiting the sensibilité of the earliest generation of Romantics, with genuine letters and autobiographical material. Bequeathed to Baron Grimm, a mangled version of the manuscript was edited by J. P. A. Parison and J. C. Brunet (Paris, 1818) as 'Mémoires et correspondance de Madame d'Épinay' with all the names changed to identify the supposed originals: Madame d'Épinay figures in it as Madame de Montbrillant, and René is generally recognized as Rousseau, Volx as Grimm, Gamier as Diderot, who is sometimes credited with major interventions in the text. The work has had a checkered career since. The only accurate edition is George Roth, ed. Les Pseudo-mémoires de Madame d'Épinay, 3 vols., 1951.
=520  \\$aLouise Florence Pétronille Tardieu d'Esclavelles d'Épinay (1726-1783), better known as Mme d'Épinay, was a French writer, a saloniste and woman of fashion, known on account of her liaisons with Friedrich Melchior, Baron von Grimm, and Jean-Jacques Rousseau, as well as her acquaintanceship with Denis Diderot, Jean le Rond d'Alembert, Baron d'Holbach and other French men of letters during the Enlightenment. She was also one of many women referenced in Simone de Beauvoir's 'The Second Sex' as an example of noble expansion of women's rights during the 18th century.
=561  \\$aEx libris Charles François de Fontanellaz (plate), lived from 1891-1956 and was editor of 'la Revue Automobile'.

=500  \\$aChristian Felix Weiße (1726–1804) a German writer and pedagogue, was among the leading representatives of the Enlightenment in Germany and is regarded as the founder of German children's literature. Four of his poems were set to music by Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart. His most lasting success were the librettos to Johann Adam Hiller's Singspiele.

=100  \\$aGoldoni, Carlo$d1707-1793$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q165534$911653
=245  \\$aScelte comedie$nvols. 1 & 2
=260  \\$aPadua$bBettoni$c1811
=300  \\$a2 vols. (332+284 pages)
=500  \\$aCarlo Osvaldo Goldoni (1707-1793) was an Italian playwright and librettist from the Republic of Venice. His works include some of Italy's most famous and best-loved plays. Audiences have admired the plays of Goldoni for their ingenious mix of wit and honesty. His plays offered his contemporaries images of themselves, often dramatizing the lives, values, and conflicts of the emerging middle classes. Though he wrote in French and Italian, his plays make rich use of the Venetian language, regional vernacular, and colloquialisms.
=500  \\$aGoldoni also wrote under the pen name and title Polisseno Fegeio, Pastor Arcade, which he claimed in his memoirs the "Arcadians of Rome" bestowed on him.
=500  \\$aThese are volumes 1 and 2 of a twelve-volume set

=041  \\$adut$hita
=100  \\$aBonarelli della Rovere, Guidubaldo$d1563-1608$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q2376577$97177
=245  \\$aFillis van Scirus. $bHerderspel van den Grave G. De Bonarelli
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bWor$bLinden, onder de$c1728
=300  \\$bfrontispiece engraving, engraved title page, illustrations$a[xvi]-285-[2] pages
=500  \\$aGuidubaldo Bonarelli wrote the pastoral drama 'Filli di Sciro' (published in 1607 but first performed in Ferrara four years earlier), a successful remake of the Leggenda di Florio e Biancofiore, whose musicality is a prelude to melodrama. The story of the drama is also intricate due to the overlapping of various love plots between the shepherd protagonists; in the end, the affair is resolved thanks to the mechanism of agnition. The genius of the plot, which struck and aroused much controversy among Bonarelli's contemporaries, was the character of the nymph in love with two shepherds, who meditated suicide because of her uncertainty. The play was a great success throughout the 17th century and was translated into French, English and Dutch
=500  \\$aTogether with Torquato Tasso's 'Aminta' and Giambattista Guarini's 'Il pastor fido', Bonarelli's 'Filli di Sciro' is considered one of the masterpieces of the genre of the pastoral drama
=500  \\$aPosthumous publication. After the author's death, Henrietta Elizabeth and Everardina Jakoba de With made sure that what remained of their sister's work was published. Thus, as early as 1728, Fillis van Scirus was published, supplemented by her Mengeldichten. The dedication of both sisters to Pieter Vlaming suggests that the latter had visited Katharina shortly before her death and that she had asked him to dedicate Fillis to him. 
=500  \\$aSecond part of the book contains ca.100 pages of poetry by de With (pastoral poems, fishermen's poems, funeral poems, and 'Mengeldichten')
=500  \\$aBound in with 'De getrouwe herderin' and ‘Gedichten’
=500  \\$aBeautiful full page illustrations at the start of each of the 5 acts, engraved by and after Jan Goeree (1670-1731)

=500  \\$aCharacter studies with beautiful, theatrical, rich and funny full-page anonymous engravings. 
=500  \\$aConlin began his literary activity in 1705. By 1711 he had written his seven-volume 'Fool's World'. With moralising and entertaining intentions, human behaviour is caricatured and illustrated by "more than 200 amusing and ridiculous incidents", "which can be usefully employed not only by the priests on the cantzel / but also by every private citizen / among honest societies". The series was concluded in 1709 and 1711 with two volumes on foolish women entitled Der Christliche Welt-Weise Beweinet Die Thorheit Derer in diesem Buch beschriebener 25. Närrinnen. 
=500  \\$aInspired by Abraham a Santa Clara (1644-1709), the famous Augustinian priest and court preacher in Vienna, and his book 'Wonderful Dream of a Great Nest of Fools' - 1703 (pub. 1710)

=501  \\$aBound in with 'Der Christliche Welt-Weise', vol. 3
=590  \\$aWelcher die in disem Buch befindliche Narrn zimblich durch die Hächel ziecht, jedoch alles mit sittlicher Lehr und H. Schrifft untermischet : Worin über 200. lustig und lächerliche Begebenheiten, deren sich nit allein die Herrn Pfarrer auf der Cantzel, sondern auch ein jede Privat-Persohn, bey ehrlichen Gesellschafften nutzlich bedienen können.

=500  \\$aCharles Collé (1709-1783) was a French dramatist and songwriter.
=500  \\$aThe 'Théâtre de société' is a collection of comedies published in 1768. It was namely for his patron, Louis Philippe I Duke of Orléans and his associates that Collé composed the greater part of his Théâtre de société. With this collection, Collé wanted to show the public his most elaborate pieces, in order to prove that he was capable of composing something other than parades, the genre in which he had become famous.

=059  \\$av
=100  \\$aPetricovius, Andreas$d15xx-1645$4edt$97198
=245  \\$aPsalterium
=260  \\$aKrakow$bPetrocovius$c1614
=300  \\$a[iv]-277-[3] pages$bWhole book printed in red and black ink, leather bound, embossed cover, metal locks, illuminated initial letters, music examples$c32x24 cm
=500  \\$amagnificent work
=500  \\$aoriginally published in 1599. Two existing examples in National Library of Poland, Warsaw, Shelfmark SD XVI. F.1000 and 1009, available online http://polona.pl
=500  \\$aThis edition of 1604 has long been assumed to be preserved in the unique copy held in the Library of Wyzsze Seminarium Duchowne in Przemysl (Shelfmark XVIII.683) See article M. Komorowska
=500  \\$aEditor of this Psalterium, Andreas Petricovius, was a lawyer, professor at the University of Krakow, doctor of philosophy and law, printer and publisher, royal secretary and servitor, Knight of the Golden Spur. The son of Andrzej the Elder, a Krakow printer and bookseller, from Piotrków, and Jadwiga née Prężyków. In 1604, he obtained a bachelor's degree in arts and philosophy at the University of Krakow, and continued his studies in Italy, France and Germany. After returning in 1615, he was delegated to Zamość to take the chair of logic at the Zamość Academy in 1620. After obtaining a doctorate in both laws at the University of Kraków, he went to Poznań, where he became rector and professor of law at the Lubrański College. A year later, after the death of his father, he returned to Kraków and entered the university's Law College. He took over his father's printing house, where he published over 230 legal (he had the exclusive right to print parliamentary constitutions), scientific and religious items.

=500  \\$aNeumeister was a German Lutheran pastor and hymnologist, and was an influential writer of texts for cantatas. Johann Sebastian Bach set his texts in some of his cantatas. Bach began setting his texts in about 1713 when he was working at Weimar. Later, while working at Köthen, he applied for a job as organist at Neumeister's church in Hamburg. 
=500  \\$aDedicated to the wives of Neumeister's colleagues Lutheran theologians Salomon Deyling (1677-1755) and Gottlieb Wernsdorf the elder (1668-1729),  respectively Louise Sibylle Wagner and Margaretha Katharina Nitzsch (1693-1764)
=500  \\$afrontispiece engraving: portrait of the author by Christian Friedrich Fritzsch (1695-1769) after Johann Salomon Wahl (1689-1765)
=590  \\$ain welchen I. Nicodemus, eine Cathechismus-Frage, II. Stephanus, eine Streit-Frage, III. Petrus, eine Gewissens-Frage, IV. Esra, eine curiöse Frage, bey allen Sonn- und Fest-Tags-Evangelien, wie auch in sieben Passions-Predigten, über Matthaei XXVI. und XXXVII. ingleichen bey Einweihung eines neuen Altars, vorgetragen. Da denn zugleich eine Unions-Schrifft, Genannt: Die nöthige Glaubens-Einigkeit der Prostestantischen Krichen, U. in der Vorrede widerlegt worden.

=500  \\$a'Neueröffneter historischer Bildersaal' was a 17-vol. book series published between 1692 and 1782. Contains numerous engravings.
=500  \\$a"About the history which took place under the reigning emperors Charles VI and Charles VII, from 1734 to 1743, especially in Europe, but also from time to time in the rest of the world and in the Church".

=500  \\$aThe target group was especially the youth, as can be seen from the title of the first edition: "Der Lehr-begierigen Jugend zu sonderbaren Nutzen und Erleuchterung also herausgegeben".
=561  \\$aEx libris Gordon Ritter (plate)
=563  \\$abound in white embossed leather, with coloured edges and metal locks
=590  \\$aDas ist: Kurtze, deutliche und impartheyische Beschreibung der Historiæ Universalis, enthaltend die Geschichte welche sich unter den Glorivürdigst-regierenden Kaysern Carolo VI und Carolo VII con dem Jahr 1734 bis auf das Jahr 1743 vornemlich in Euroa, auch sonst hin und wieder in der Welt und in der Kirche zugetragen. Durchgehends mit vielen Kupffern ausgezieret, und mit gehörigen Registern versehen.

=500  \\$aThe last section, entitled 'Sing-Gedichte' is dedicated to the “edle Musik” and contains cantata texts based on existing melodies from opera arias by Handel, Telemann, Graun, Graupner, and Hasse, on sonata movements by Johann Christoph Pepusch, and tle libretti by Uffenbach for 2 Sinspiele ('Pisitatratus' and 'Hass und Neid')
=500  \\$avon Uffenbach was a German architect, lawyer and scholar, as well as collector and patron of the arts, a librettist and music lover (he played the lute as well). Born into a wealthy bourgeois family in Frankfurt, he held high office in the city administration, was a member of the city council and in 1762 became mayor of Frankfurt.
=500  \\$aCebes of Thebes (ca. 430-350 B.C.E.) was a member of Socrates’ inner circle. One of the dialogs that has been attributed to him is the Pinax or Tabula, also known as the Tablet of Cebes. Uffenbach's book contains a magnificent folded engraving of the tablet by Matthaeus Merian: "Tabvla Cebetis Continens Totius Hvmanæ Descriptionem", an allegorical picture on which the whole of human life with its dangers and temptations was symbolically represented.

=561  \\$aEx libris Bibliotheca Acad. Georgiae Augustae (Stamp)
=590  \\$aWorinnen, nebst einer poetischen Auslegung des Sinnebildes Cebetis des Thebaners, verschiedene moralische Schrifften zu Ausbesserung menschlicher Sitten enthalten, und nebst einer Vorrede von der Würde derer Singe-Gedichte, Mit dessen Genehmhaltung an das Licht gestellet.

=041  \\$ager
=100  \\$aHarsdörffer, Georg Philipp$d1607-1658$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q66605$97319
=245  \\$aGesprachspiele, $bso bey Ehrn- und Tugendliebenden Gesellschaften aufzuüben$nvol. 3
=260  \\$aNuremberg$bEndter$c1643
=300  \\$a[xvii]-472-[48] pages$bmusic examples, illustrations$c9x14 cm, oblong
=500  \\$aContains plates (title-page, Erklärung, biv, 2, 20, 21, 156, 157, 159, 160, 162-164, 166, 167, 169-175, 185, 192, 200, 204, 212, 233, 241, 248, 251, 264, 266, 268, 346, 350, 353, and last page) and music
=500  \\$aSome notes in German handwriting in inner cover
=500  \\$aInfluenced by the French ideal of the "honnête homme", the "informed and socially polished type of man", in his "Frauenzimmer Gesprächspielen" the Nuremberg native takes his cue not least from the model and content of the public "Conférences" in Paris - the kind of informal gathering in which representatives of fiction and the education-hungry middle class, but no less so representatives of the natural sciences, debate "all the fine matters of physics, morals, mathematics and other disciplines". Because they combine "information and narration" in a variety of ways, combine "knowledge and intellectual pleasure", take the "delectare" of the ancient and humanistic dual purpose of literature alongside the "prodesse" really seriously, one rightly sees a "conversational aesthetic of 'impromptu'" at work in the layout of the "Gesprächspiele". These mind games of intellectual sociability were also part of the Italian Academies (such as the "Intronati", "Incogniti" and "Oziosi") Harsdörffer got in contact with during his Italian travels. Subjects of all kind are discussed in the form of a free conversation in which six persons, of both sexes and different ages, take part. 
=500  \\$aSubjects of all kind are discussed in the guise of a free conversation in which six persons, of both sexes and different ages, take part. A great number of fine copperplates, some emblematic, others taken from contemporary life, illustrate the text, so that the work has become a treasure house for literary research.
=500  \\$aConversation CXXX (p.170-242) seems to be a musical drama entitled 'Von der Welt Eitelkeit', offering information on libretto, cast, stagesets, music (instrumentation, score) & lighting. As the opera (allegorical shepherd's play) 'Seelewig' is found in the fourth volume on a libretto by Harsdörffer himself, and music composed by Sigmund Theophil Staden (1607-1655), this could probably be by the same team.
=500  \\$aFront plate (double paged) represents the company of six persons (a quartet and a duo) walking in a courtyard of a beautiful villa under a starry night sky, far from the world, as they turn to erudite, entertaining, perceptive conversation.
=534  \\$aThe 8 volumes of "(Frauenzimmer) Gesprachspiele" were published periodically (1643-1649), though not at regular intervals, and may thus be regarded as the forerunner of a literary magazine. Beginning with vol. 3 the word 'Frauenzimmer' is omitted, presumably in order not to frighten away male readers. 
=561  \\$aEx libris N. Ferber Hamburg 1876 (manuscript) and Dr. Med. Ferber 1882 (plate)

=041  \\$adut
=245  \\$aVaderlandsche liederen voor het Genootschap van Wapenhandel,$b ter spreuk voerende: Voor Vrijheid en Vaderland $n1-6/6
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aLeiden$bHeyligert$c1784-86
=300  \\$a6 vols. (40+38+44+40+40+40 pages)$b1 folded page musical example
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aCollection of Dutch patriotic songs
=500  \\$aThe "Schutterijen" in the cities of the Dutch Republic, were traditionally militias, citizen's rifle companies organised as guilds. 
Civilian armament was one of the tenets of the Patriot movement of the 1780s, which resulted in either the existing civic militias being put at the service of the Patriot movement or, in addition to the traditional militias, new companies were established under names such as 'exercitiegenootschappen' or 'genootschap tot de wapenhandel' (arms trade). (Arms trade here means the handling of weapons).

=500  \\$aThe Patriot movement set a lot of songwriters' pens in motion, among others:
Vaderlandsche liederen voor het Genootschap van Wapenhandel ter spreuke gevoerd 'Voor Vrijheid en Vaderland', of which the first volume appeared in 1784. Five sequels appeared in the following years. They included works by Pieter Vreede (1750-1837) and by Pieter van Schelle (1749-1792), F. van Aken, J. 't Hooft Jz. and others. 
=500  \\$aIn the Patriot songs, a number of themes recur regularly: freedom fighters from the classical and recent past, freedom and patriotism, the marching bands, events from the short history of the Patriot movement, the leaders of the Patriot movement, Christian themes of justice, and - in an antagonistic sense - the stadholder and his allies.

=500  \\$a Collection of Dutch patriotic songs

=500  \\$aThe "Schutterijen" in the cities of the Dutch Republic, were traditionally militias, citizen's rifle companies organised as guilds.
Civilian armament was one of the tenets of the Patriot movement of the 1780s, which resulted in either the existing civic militias being put at the service of the Patriot movement or, in addition to the traditional militias, new companies were established under names such as 'exercitiegenootschappen' or 'genootschap tot de wapenhandel' (arms trade). (Arms trade here means the handling of weapons).

=500  \\$aThe Patriot movement set a lot of songwriters' pens in motion, among others:
'Vaderlandsche liederen voor het Genootschap van Wapenhandel' - of which the first volume appeared in 1784 & five sequels appeared in the following years - and 'Batavian songs for the free Dutch' published in Amsterdam for the society 'Tot Nut der Schutterij' (To the benefit of the militia) in 1785.
=500  \\$aIn the Patriot songs, a number of themes recur regularly: 
freedom fighters from the classical and recent past, freedom and patriotism, the marching bands, events from the short history of the Patriot movement, the leaders of the Patriot movement, Christian themes of justice, and - in an antagonistic sense - the stadholder and his allies.

=100  \\$aSwift, Jonathan$d1667-1745$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q41166$97332
=245  \\$aLe Conte du tonneau
=250  \\$aRev. ed.
=260  \\$aThe Hague$bScheurleer$c1741
=300  \\$a2 vols. ([xxiv]-300-[14]+[xiv]-286-[10] pages), 7 pages of plates$bTitle pages in red & black ink, engraved frontispiece, 7 inserted engraved plates
=520  \\$aA 'Tale of a Tub' (see also X1C18) was first published by the Irish clergyman and novelist Jonathan Swift in 1704; it is the first and perhaps most difficult of all his satires. The title is thought to refer to a dissenting priest’s pulpit, and the work is a biting parody on the religious extravagances that Swift perceived among the clergy at the start of the 18th century. The narrative is written using a complex though playful technique of interlinking stories concerning the lives of three brothers. particularly noteworthy for the woodcut illustrations that punctuate the text. For example, there is a striking image of a priest reprimanding the congregation down below, with a gallows and theatre shown in the background. The frontispiece also illustrates a whale distracted by a barrel thrown overboard by sailors: an allegory, perhaps, of how the text was designed to draw the attention of political and religious dissenters away from the affairs of the ‘ship’ of state.

=245  \\$aReflexions critiques sur la poésie et sur la peinture
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aParis$bMariette$c1719
=300  \\$a2 vols. ([viii]-692+[xii]-529-[2] pages)
=520  \\$aThe Réflexions critiques sur la poésie et sur la peinture is a work on the theory of art, the theory of literature and the theory of music by Jean-Baptiste Dubos, first published in 1719 and often republished since.
Taking Horace's hemistiche Ut pictura poesis as its epigraph, the Réflexions critiques sur la poésie et sur la peinture marked a turning point in aesthetic thought and was to exert a considerable influence on the development of theatrical art and music throughout the Enlightenment.

=100  \\$aGlazemaker, Jan Hendrik$d1620-1682$4trl$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q2221565$97337
=245  \\$aToonneel der wereltsche veranderingen.$bdoor deftige, vermakelijke en ware geschiedenissen afgebeelt,$n1-2/2
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bHilten, van; Doornick$c1648; 1659
=300  \\$a2 vols. ([viii]-554 + [viii]-562 pages)$bbound in white vellum, illustrations, engraved title page
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$avol. 1 is published by van Hilten, vol. 2 by Doornik
=500  \\$aGlazemaker was a Dutch translator of almost 70 books, mostly from Latin and from French. Glazemaker probably lived and worked in Amsterdam, where most of his translations were published. He may have been the first person in history to make a living primarily by translating into Dutch. While much of his output was of the Latin classics, he was particularly noted for his translations of the writings of René Descartes from both French and Latin.
=500  \\$aA considerable number of the stories are translations of writings by the highly productive Bishop of Belley, Jean Pierre Camus, who in that first half of the century published some 960 short stories - in 21 collections - in addition to another 15 more or less substantial novels. Bishop at the age of 25, Camus felt called upon to counterbalance all the frivolities and absurdities he felt were appearing in this field with his stories and novels. The stories he published pretended to be true, since they were presented as examples of how things can go wrong when a person does not comply with Christian standards of a good life. To this end, they were usually provided with edifying introductions and conclusions. Glazemaker omitted these in his translations, which, had he known it, would undoubtedly have saddened Camus greatly. This left relatively short accounts of murders, rapes, adulteries and so on, which the reader was supposed to assume really happened, just as the reader of a newspaper is supposed to believe in the reality of mixed messages. But in between, Glazemaker included stories in his collection that apparently did not care about whether they really happened but about how striking the story is.

=500  \\$aA collection of three very popular tales (Le sottilissime astutie di Bertoldo, Le piacevoli et ridicolose simplicità di Bertoldino and Novella di Cacasenno, figliuolo del semplice Bertoldino), the first two written by Giulio Cesare Croce and the last by Adriano Banchieri (under the pseudonym of Camillo Scaliggeri della Fratta), first published in 1620. The tales take up and rework ancient novellas, in particular the medieval 'Disputa di Salomone con Marcolfo'. 
=500  \\$aBased on this editition : Bertoldo, Bertoldino e Cacasenno, opera buffa by Vincenzo Legrenzio Ciampi to a libretto by Carlo Goldoni, premiered on 26 December 1748 at the Teatro San Moisè in Venice and entered the repertoire of the Académie royale de musique in Paris on 9 November 1753 under the title Bertoldo in corte
=500  \\$aGiulio Cesare Croce was an Italian writer, actor/producer of cantastoria and enigma writer. He had an enormous success with his story telling and was able to travel to fairs, markets, patrician houses, and the Italian courts. His presentations were complemented by a violin. His prolific literary production was contingent upon his own transcriptions of his shows.

=100  \\$aGottsched, Johann Christoph$d1700-1766$4aut$4win$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q76442$910582
=245  \\$aDer deutschen Gesellschaft in Leipzig gesammlete Reden und Gedichte $bwelchen bey dem Eintritte und Abschiede ihrer Mitglieder Pflegen abgelesen zu werden.
=260  \\$aLeipzig$bBreitkopf$c1732
=300  \\$a[xl]-424 pages
=500  \\$aThe German Society was a language society in Leipzig in the late Baroque and Enlightenment periods. Their goals included the promotion of the German language and its emancipation from Latin and French, and later the enforcement of the New High German written language throughout the German-speaking area. After its most prominent member, Johann Christoph Gottsched, left in a dispute, the society quickly lost importance. In 1945 it was dissolved.

=500  \\$acontains manuscript role list of actors/singerd involved in the Amsterdam Schouwburg productions of 1792 and 1795
=500  \\$aThe plot concerns Silvain, who works as a poor farmer after being disinherited by his rich father for marrying a lower-class woman. The pastoral theme and its celebration of rural life was common in opéra-comique of the time but Marmontel's libretto goes much further in advocating social equality and defending the rights of peasants against the encroachment of landowners.

=100  \\$aHirsch, Paul$d1881-1951$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q2060211$4col$4edt$97450
=245  \\$aKatalog der Musikbibliothek Paul Hirsch, Frankfurt am Main$nvols. 3-4
=260  \\$aFrankfurt am Main$aCambridge$bHirsch$bCambridge University Press$c1936$c1947
=300  \\$a2 vols. ([vii-362 + xxiii-695 pages)$bplates, illustrations, facsililes, music examples, photographs
=500  \\$aPaul Adolf Hirsch was a German industrialist. He was also a musician, bibliophile and musicologist who assembled the largest private music library in Europe. The Hirsch Collection is now housed at the British Library.
=500  \\$aHirsch, an accomplished violinist, took a keen interest in publications concerning all aspects of music—performance, history and theory. In 1896 he began to collect historical musical works, focusing on early printed editions of Haydn, Mozart and Beethoven, 19th-century opera and early theoretical works. In 1922 Hirsch hired musicologist Kathi Meyer (later Meyer-Baer) as a research assistant and opened the library to the public two days a week. Hirsch and Meyer began compiling a catalog of the library contents. 
=500  \\$aThe first three volumes were originally published by Martin Breslauer, Berlin, and were reprinted by Morsum/Sylt:Cicero Presse of Hamburg in 1993. The fourth volume, which includes addenda to the first three, was completed in Cambridge with the help of Edith Schnapper and Hirsch's daughters, Irene Hartogs-Hirsch and Renate Schuster.
Vol. 1: Theoretische Drucke bis 1800. (1928)
Vol. 2: Opern-Partituren. (1930)
Vol. 3: Instrumental- und Vokalmusik bis etwa 1830. (1936)
Vol. 4: Erstausgaben, Chorwerke in Partitur, Gesamtausgaben, Nachschlagewerke etc. Ergänzungen zu Bd. 1–3. Cambridge University Press (1947)
=500  \\$aVol. 3, subtitled "Instrumental- und Vokalmusik bis etwa 1830", was published in 1936 in Frankfurt a.M., in the series 'Veröffentlichungen der Musikbibliothek Paul Hirsch', 2. series, vol. 3
=500  \\$avol. 4, subtitled "Erstausgaben, Chorwerke in Partitur, Gesamtausgaben, Nachschlagwerke etc. Ergänzungen zu Bd. I-III" was published in 1947 in Cambridge
=500  \\$aVol. 4 contains an autograph dedication to Alex Hyatt King:" "... That place, that does contain my books, the best companions, is to me a glorious court, where hourly I converse with the old sages and philosophers..." (John Fletcher). If my friend Alex. H. King replaces the word "old" by "young", this should be a very apt inscription for this copy of my Volume IV. London, at the B.M., January 6th, 1948, Paul Hirsch"
=504  \\$aVol.4 contains indexes
=561  \\$aVol. 4 contains an autograph dedication to Alex Hyatt King
=563  \\$aBound in white vellum, with cardboard front and back cover
